The log manager applies two metrics to identify segments which are\\n154:         eligible for deletion: time and size. For time-based policies, the record timestamps are considered, with the\\n155:         largest timestamp in a segment file (order of records is not relevant) defining the retention time for the\\n156:         entire segment. Size-based retention is disabled by default. When enabled the log manager keeps deleting the\\n157:         oldest segment file until the overall size of the partition is within the configured limit again. If both\\n158:         policies are enabled at the same time, a segment that is eligible for deletion due to either policy will be\\n159:         deleted. To avoid locking reads while still allowing deletes that modify the segment list we use a copy-on-write\\n160:         style segment list implementation that provides consistent views to allow a binary search to proceed on an\\n161: ... The log manager applies two metrics to identify segments which are\n154:         eligible for deletion: time and size. For time-based policies, the record timestamps are considered, with the\n155:         largest timestamp in a segment file (order of records is not relevant) defining the retention time for the\n156:         entire segment. Size-based retention is disabled by default. When enabled the log manager keeps deleting the\n157:         oldest segment file until the overall size of the partition is within the configured limit again. If both\n158:         policies are enabled at the same time, a segment that is eligible for deletion due to either policy will be\n159:         deleted. To avoid locking reads while still allowing deletes that modify the segment list we use a copy-on-write\n160:         style segment list implementation that provides consistent views to allow a binary search to proceed on an\n161: ... responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \\\"compact\\\" retention strategy.\\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\\n52:  * <p>\\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \\\"clean\\\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\\n54:  * \\\"dirty\\\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \\\"cleanable\\\" section followed by an \\\"uncleanable\\\" section.\\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\\n57:  * <p>\\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \\\"compact\\\" retention policy\\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\\n60:  * <p>\\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\\n63:  * <p>\\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\\n69:  * <p>\\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\\n71:  * <p>\\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\\n82:  * are the key points:\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * <ol>\\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\\n96:  * </ol>\\n97:  */\\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\\n99:     private static final Logger CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_BACKOFF_MS_PROP\\n109:     );\\n110: \\n111:     // Visible for test\\n112:     public static final String MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = private static final String DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"DeadThreadCount\\\";\\n118: \\n119:     // Visible for test\\n120:     public static final Set<String> METRIC_NAMES = Set.of(\\n121:             MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n122:             CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n123:             MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME,\\n124: responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \\\"compact\\\" retention strategy.\\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\\n52:  * <p>\\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \\\"clean\\\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\\n54:  * \\\"dirty\\\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \\\"cleanable\\\" section followed by an \\\"uncleanable\\\" section.\\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\\n57:  * <p>\\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \\\"compact\\\" retention policy\\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\\n60:  * <p>\\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\\n63:  * <p>\\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\\n69:  * <p>\\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\\n71:  * <p>\\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\\n82:  * are the key points:\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * <ol>\\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\\n96:  * </ol>\\n97:  */\\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\\n99:     private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\\n100: \\n101:     public static final Set<String> RECONFIGURABLE_CONFIGS = Set.of(\\n102:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_THREADS_PROP,\\n103:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_DEDUPE_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\\n104:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_DEDUPE_BUFFER_LOAD_FACTOR_PROP,\\n105:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\\n106:             ServerConfigs.MESSAGE_MAX_BYTES_CONFIG,\\n107:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_MAX_BYTES_PER_SECOND_PROP,\\n108:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_BACKOFF_MS_PROP\\n109:     );\\n110: \\n111:     // Visible for test\\n112:     public static final String MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"max-buffer-utilization-percent\\\";\\n113:     public static final String MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME = \\\"max-clean-time-secs\\\";\\n114:     public static final String MAX_COMPACTION_DELAY_METRICS_NAME = \\\"max-compaction-delay-secs\\\";\\n115: \\n116:     private static final String CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"cleaner-recopy-percent\\\";\\n117:     private static final String DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME = \\\"DeadThreadCount\\\";\\n118: \\n119:     // Visible for test\\n120:     public static final Set<String> METRIC_NAMES = Set.of(\\n121:             MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n122:             CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n123:             MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME,\\n124:             MAX_COMPACTION_DELAY_METRICS_NAME,\\n125:             DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME\\n126:     );\\n127: \\n128:     // For compatibility, metrics are defined to be under `kafka.log.LogCleaner` class\\n129:     private final KafkaMetricsGroup metricsGroup = new KafkaMetricsGroup(\\\"kafka.log\\\", \\\"LogCleaner\\\");\\n130: \\n131:     /**\\n132:      * For managing the state of partitions being cleaned.\\n133:      */\\n134:     private final LogCleanerManager cleanerManager;\\n135: \\n136:     /**\\n137:      * A throttle used to limit the I/O of all the cleaner threads to a @SuppressWarnings(\\\"this-escape\\\")\\n158:     public LogCleaner(CleanerConfig initialConfig,\\n159:                       List<File> logDirs,\\n160:     registerMetrics();\\n171:     }\\n172: \\n173:     private void registerMetrics() {\\n174:         /* a metric to track the maximum utilization of any thread's buffer in the last cleaning */\\n175:         metricsGroup.newGauge(MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\\n176:                 () -> (int) (maxOverCleanerThreads(t -> t.lastStats.bufferUtilization) * 100));\\n177: \\n178:         /* a metric to track the recopy rate of each thread's last cleaning */\\n179:         metricsGroup.newGauge(CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME, () -> {\\n180:             List<CleanerStats> stats = cleaners.stream().map(t -> t.lastStats).toList();\\n181:             double recopyRate = (double) stats.stream().mapToLong(stat -> stat.bytesWritten).sum() /\\n182:                     Math.max(stats.stream().mapToLong(stat -> stat.bytesRead).sum(), 1);\\n183:             return (int) (100 * recopyRate);\\n184:         });\\n185: \\n186:         /* a metric to track the thread.shutdown();\\n226:             } catch (InterruptedException e) {\\n227:                 throw new RuntimeException(e);\\n228:             }\\n229:         });\\n230:         cleaners.clear();\\n231:     }\\n232: \\n233:     /**\\n234:      * Stop the background cleaner threads.\\n235:      */\\n236:     public void shutdown() {\\n237:         try {\\n238: of configs that is reconfigurable in LogCleaner\\n254:      */\\n255:     @Override\\n256:     public Set<String> reconfigurableConfigs() {\\n257:         return RECONFIGURABLE_CONFIGS;\\n258:     }\\n259: \\n260:     /**\\n261:      * Validate the new cleaner threads num is reasonable.\\n262:      *\\n263:      * @param newConfig A submitted new AbstractConfig instance that contains new cleaner config\\n264:      */\\n265:     @Override\\n266:     public void validateReconfiguration(AbstractConfig newConfig) {\\n267:         int numThreads = new current value \\\" + currentThreads);\\n275: \\n276:     }\\n277: \\n278:     /**\\n279:      * Reconfigure log clean config. Each thread processes does its cleaning repeatedly by\\n465:      * choosing the dirtiest log, cleaning it, and then swapping in the cleaned segments.\\n466:      */\\n467:     public class CleanerThread extends ShutdownableThread {\\n468:         private final Logger logger = new LogContext(logPrefix).logger(CleanerThread.class);\\n469: \\n470:         private final Cleaner cleaner;\\n471: \\n472:         private volatile CleanerStats lastStats = new CleanerStats(Time.SYSTEM);\\n473:         private volatile PreCleanStats lastPreCleanStats = new PreCleanStats();\\n474: \\n475:         @SuppressWarnings(\\\"this-escape\\\")\\n476:         public CleanerThread(int threadId) throws NoSuchAlgorithmException {\\n477:             super(\\\"kafka-log-cleaner-thread-\\\" + threadId, false);\\n478: \\n479:             cleaner = new Cleaner(\\n480:                     threadId,\\n481:                     new SkimpyOffsetMap((int) Math.min(config.dedupeBufferSize / config.numThreads, Integer.MAX_VALUE), config.hashAlgorithm()),\\n482:                     config.ioBufferSize / config.numThreads / 2,\\n483:                     config.maxMessageSize,\\n484:                     config.dedupeBufferLoadFactor,\\n485:                     throttler,\\n486:                     time,\\n487:                     this::checkDone\\n488:             );\\n489: \\n490:             if (config.dedupeBufferSize / config.numThreads > Integer.MAX_VALUE) {\\n491:                 logger.warn(\\\"Cannot use more than 2G of cleaner buffer space per cleaner thread, ignoring excess buffer space...\\\");\\n492:             }\\n493:         }\\n494: \\n495:         /**\\n496:          *  Check if the cleaning for a partition is aborted. \\n550:                 return false;\\n551:             }\\n552:         }\\n553: \\n554:         private boolean cleanFilthiestLog() throws LogCleaningException {\\n555:             PreCleanStats preCleanStats = new PreCleanStats();\\n556:             Optional<LogToClean> ltc = cleanerManager.grabFilthiestCompactedLog(time, preCleanStats);\\n557:             boolean cleaned;\\n558: \\n559:             if (ltc.isEmpty()) {\\n560:                 cleaned = false;\\n561:             } else {\\n562:                 // there's a log, clean it\\n563:                 this.lastPreCleanStats = preCleanStats;\\n564:                 LogToClean cleanable = ltc.get();\\n565:                 try {\\n566:                     cleanLog(cleanable);\\n567:                     cleaned = true;\\n568:                 } catch (ThreadShutdownException e) {\\n569:                     throw e;\\n570:                 } catch (Exception e) {\\n571:                     throw new LogCleaningException(cleanable.log(), e.getMessage(), e);\\n572:                 }\\n573:             }\\n574: \\n575:             Map<TopicPartition, UnifiedLog> deletable = cleanerManager.deletableLogs();\\n576:             try {\\n577:                 deletable.forEach((topicPartition, log) -> {\\n578:                     try {\\n579:                         log.deleteOldSegments();\\n580:                     } catch (ThreadShutdownException e) {\\n581:                         throw e;\\n582:                     } catch (Exception e) {\\n583:                         throw new LogCleaningException(log, e.getMessage(), e);\\n584:                     }\\n585:                 });\\n586:             } finally {\\n587:                 cleanerManager.doneDeleting(deletable.keySet().stream().toList());\\n588:             }\\n589: \\n590:             return cleaned;\\n591:         }\\n592: \\n593:         private void cleanLog(LogToClean cleanable) throws DigestException {\\n594:             long startOffset = cleanable.firstDirtyOffset();\\n595:             long endOffset = startOffset;\\n596:             try {\\n597:                 Map.Entry<Long, CleanerStats> entry = cleaner.clean(cleanable);\\n598:                 endOffset = entry.getKey();\\n599:                 recordStats(cleaner.id(), cleanable.log().name(), startOffset, endOffset, entry.getValue());\\n600:             } catch (LogCleaningAbortedException ignored) {\\n601:                 // task can be aborted, let it go.\\n602:             } catch (KafkaStorageException ignored) {\\n603:                 // partition is already offline. let it go.\\n604:             } catch (IOException e) {\\n605:                 String logDirectory = cleanable.log().parentDir();\\n606:                 String msg = String.format(\\\"Failed to clean up log for %s in dir %s due to IOException\\\", cleanable.topicPartition(), logDirectory);\\n607:                 logDirFailureChannel.maybeAddOfflineLogDir(logDirectory, msg, e);\\n608:             } finally {\\n609:                 cleanerManager.doneCleaning(cleanable.topicPartition(), cleanable.log().parentDirFile(), endOffset);\\n610:             }\\n611:         }\\n612: \\n613:         /**\\n614:          * Log out statistics on a single run of the cleaner.\\n615:          *\\n616:          * @param id The cleaner thread id\\n617:          * @param name The cleaned log name\\n618:          * @param from The java.util.stream.Collectors;\n47: import java.util.stream.IntStream;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \"compact\" retention strategy.\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \"clean\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\n54:  * \"dirty\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \"cleanable\" section followed by an \"uncleanable\" section.\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\n57:  * <p>\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \"compact\" retention policy\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\n60:  * <p>\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\n63:  * <p>\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\n66:  * <p>\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\n69:  * <p>\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\n71:  * <p>\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n73:  * <p>\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n80:  * <p>\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\n82:  * are the key points:\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * <ol>\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\n96:  * </ol>\n97:  */\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\n99:     private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\n100: \n101:     public static final Set<String> RECONFIGURABLE_CONFIGS = Set.of(\n102:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_THREADS_PROP,\n103:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_DEDUPE_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\n104:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_DEDUPE_BUFFER_LOAD_FACTOR_PROP,\n105:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\n106:             ServerConfigs.MESSAGE_MAX_BYTES_CONFIG,\n107:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_MAX_BYTES_PER_SECOND_PROP,\n108:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_BACKOFF_MS_PROP\n109:     );\n110: \n111:     // Visible for test\n112:     public static final String MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \"max-buffer-utilization-percent\";\n113:     public static final String components: the cleaner thread, segment selection policy, and key-based deduplication logic.\\n\\n**Cleaner Thread**: The LogCleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaner.java) manages a pool of CleanerThread instances that continuously perform background log cleaning. Each CleanerThread inherits from ShutdownableThread and executes the main cleaning loop via the doWork() method, which alternates between cleaning the filthiest log and pausing when no cleanable logs exist.\\n\\n**Segment Selection Policy**: The LogCleanerManager class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java) implements the segment selection policy through the grabFilthiestCompactedLog() method. This method selects logs for cleaning based on the \\\"cleanable ratio\\\" - the ratio of dirty bytes to total bytes. The method filters for logs with compact retention policy that are not already in progress, calculates cleanable offsets via cleanableOffsets(), and returns the log with the highest cleanable ratio. This ensures the dirtiest logs are cleaned first, optimizing I/O usage.\\n\\n**Key-Based Deduplication Logic**: The actual deduplication happens in the Cleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/Cleaner.java). The key methods are:\\n\\n1. buildOffsetMap() (line 635-681) - Constructs a key=>last_offset mapping for the dirty section of the log using the OffsetMap interface.\\n\\n2. SkimpyOffsetMap implementation (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/SkimpyOffsetMap.java) - A hash table using cryptographic hashing (MD5 by default) to deduplicate keys with collision resolution via probing. The put() method (line 134-164) stores key hashes and offsets, updating existing entries or adding new ones. The get() method (line 107-126) retrieves the offset for a given key hash.\\n\\n3. shouldRetainRecord() method (line 492-527) - The core deduplication logic that determines if a record should be retained during cleaning. It checks if the record has the latest offset for its key using the offset map. Records are retained if they have a value or cannot be deleted yet (based on delete retention policies).\\n\\n4. cleanInto() method (line 306-415) - Uses a MemoryRecords.RecordFilter to iterate through source records and apply the shouldRetainRecord() logic, filtering out obsolete records and writing retained records to the cleaned segment.\\n\\n5. groupSegmentsBySize() method (line 566-601) - Selects which segments to group together during cleaning, ensuring groups don't exceed maximum log/index sizes to prevent excessive segment shrinkage.\\n\\nThe cleaning flow: CleanerThread.doWork() → grabFilthiestCompactedLog() → Cleaner.clean() → buildOffsetMap() → cleanSegments() → cleanInto() → shouldRetainRecord() using SkimpyOffsetMap for fast lookups of the latest offset for each key.\\n\\nSupporting classes include CleanerConfig (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanerConfig.java) for configuration, CleanerStats and PreCleanStats for metrics, LogCleaningState (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaningState.java) for state management, LogToClean (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogToClean.java) representing a log to clean, and CleanedTransactionMetadata (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanedTransactionMetadata.java) for managing transaction state during cleaning.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":458,"cache_read_input_tokens":104756,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":458},"output_tokens":6,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cdc4cb47-f20b-45bc-88c6-c015a70ecada","uuid":"ffedd12a-993a-4fb0-aaac-a15a8579fa69"}

components: the cleaner thread, segment selection policy, and key-based deduplication logic.\\n\\n**Cleaner Thread**: The LogCleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaner.java) manages a pool of CleanerThread instances that continuously perform background log cleaning. Each CleanerThread inherits from ShutdownableThread and executes the main cleaning loop via the doWork() method, which alternates between cleaning the filthiest log and pausing when no cleanable logs exist.\\n\\n**Segment Selection Policy**: The LogCleanerManager class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java) implements the segment selection policy through the grabFilthiestCompactedLog() method. This method selects logs for cleaning based on the \\\"cleanable ratio\\\" - the ratio of dirty bytes to total bytes. The method filters for logs with compact retention policy that are not already in progress, calculates cleanable offsets via cleanableOffsets(), and returns the log with the highest cleanable ratio. This ensures the dirtiest logs are cleaned first, optimizing I/O usage.\\n\\n**Key-Based Deduplication Logic**: The actual deduplication happens in the Cleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/Cleaner.java). The key methods are:\\n\\n1. buildOffsetMap() (line 635-681) - Constructs a key=>last_offset mapping for the dirty section of the log using the OffsetMap interface.\\n\\n2. SkimpyOffsetMap implementation (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/SkimpyOffsetMap.java) - A hash table using cryptographic hashing (MD5 by default) to deduplicate keys with collision resolution via probing. The put() method (line 134-164) stores key hashes and offsets, updating existing entries or adding new ones. The get() method (line 107-126) retrieves the offset for a given key hash.\\n\\n3. shouldRetainRecord() method (line 492-527) - The core deduplication logic that determines if a record should be retained during cleaning. It checks if the record has the latest offset for its key using the offset map. Records are retained if they have a value or cannot be deleted yet (based on delete retention policies).\\n\\n4. cleanInto() method (line 306-415) - Uses a MemoryRecords.RecordFilter to iterate through source records and apply the shouldRetainRecord() logic, filtering out obsolete records and writing retained records to the cleaned segment.\\n\\n5. groupSegmentsBySize() method (line 566-601) - Selects which segments to group together during cleaning, ensuring groups don't exceed maximum log/index sizes to prevent excessive segment shrinkage.\\n\\nThe cleaning flow: CleanerThread.doWork() → grabFilthiestCompactedLog() → Cleaner.clean() → buildOffsetMap() → cleanSegments() → cleanInto() → shouldRetainRecord() using SkimpyOffsetMap for fast lookups of the latest offset for each key.\\n\\nSupporting classes include CleanerConfig (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanerConfig.java) for configuration, CleanerStats and PreCleanStats for metrics, LogCleaningState (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaningState.java) for state management, LogToClean (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogToClean.java) representing a log to clean, and CleanedTransactionMetadata (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanedTransactionMetadata.java) for managing transaction state during cleaning.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
